## lattice-system

A Lean 4 + Mathlib formalization project targeting general lattice models.
This project subsumes and generalizes the earlier
[ising-model](https://github.com/phasetr/ising-model) project, progressively
covering classical spin systems, quantum spin systems, Hubbard, BCS,
CAR algebras, and eventually lattice QCD.

## Design axis: graphs, not lattices

Despite the name, the **primary combinatorial abstraction in this
library is a graph `(خ›, E_خ›)`** â€” finite for finite-volume work and
infinite for the thermodynamic-limit / algebraic-formulation work
that is a major long-term goal â€” not "a lattice". Concrete lattices
(the 1D chain, square / cubic grids, infinite chains, â„¤^d, â€¦) appear
only as specific instances such as `SimpleGraph.pathGraph`,
`SimpleGraph.cycleGraph`, products of these, or their infinite
analogues. This convention follows the standard mathematical-physics
literature on many-body systems on graphs (Lieb's theorem on
bipartite lattices, the Marshallâ€“Liebâ€“Mattis theorem, Miyao 2021
آ§3, â€¦) and aligns the project with mathlib's `SimpleGraph`
foundations.

Finite-volume work uses `خ› : Type*` together with `[Fintype خ›]`
when needed (e.g. for traces, partition functions, finite sums of
local terms); infinite-volume work drops the `Fintype` assumption
and uses graphs over types like `â„¤` or `â„¤^d` instead.

The bridge from a `SimpleGraph` to the pairwise coupling
`J : خ› â†’ خ› â†’ â„‚` consumed by `heisenbergHamiltonian` (and similar
operators) lives in `LatticeSystem.Lattice.Graph` (`couplingOf`).
Existing chain coupling families (`openChainCoupling`,
`periodicChainCoupling`) are characterised as
`couplingOf (pathGraph _) _` and `couplingOf (cycleGraph _) _`
respectively.

## Scope

| Area | Stage | Typical references |
|---|---|---|
| Classical spin systems | Inherited from ising-model | Friedli-Velenik, Glimm-Jaffe |
| Quantum spin systems | Current focus | Tasaki, Nielsen-Chuang (cross-check) |
| Hubbard / BCS | Medium term | Tasaki 1998, Bru-Pedra |
| CAR-algebraic formulation | Medium-long term | Araki-Moriya, Bru-Pedra |
| Thermodynamic limit (infinite graphs) | Long term, **major project goal** | Simon, Friedli-Velenik, Bratteli-Robinson |
| Lattice QCD | Longest term | Aarts, Davies |

## Refactoring conventions and review criteria

A **single-source-of-truth document** for refactoring conventions
applied as the review checklist on every pull request:
[Refactoring conventions and review criteria](refactoring-conventions.html).
Topics: test methods (decide / bridge / small-exhaustive / shim /
`#guard_msgs`), module-split criteria, generic / dedup conventions,
deprecation window policy, naming / docstring rules, linter
exceptions, public-doc synchronisation.

The companion page [Deprecation window](deprecations.html) tracks
currently-deprecated public declarations, the `since` date,
recommended replacement, and earliest-removal window.

## Formalized theorems

All items below are formally proved with **zero `sorry`**. Full
mathematical statements and proof sketches are in
[`tex/proof-guide.tex`](https://github.com/phasetr/lattice-system/blob/main/tex/proof-guide.tex).

### Single-site Pauli operators

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, آ§2.1 eq. (2.1.8), p. 15. Cross-checked with Nielsen-Chuang
آ§2.1.3 Figure 2.2 (pp. 65-66, definitions), Ex. 2.19 (p. 70,
Hermiticity), Ex. 2.41 (p. 78, `(دƒ^خ±)آ² = I` and anticommutation),
Ex. 2.40 (p. 77, commutator, whence the cyclic products).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `pauliX/Y/Z_isHermitian` | `(دƒ^خ±)â€  = دƒ^خ±` | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |
| `pauliX/Y/Z_mul_self` | `(دƒ^خ±)آ² = I` | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |
| `pauliX_mul_pauliY` etc. | `دƒ^x دƒ^y = iآ·دƒ^z` (cyclic) | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |
| `pauliX_anticomm_pauliY` etc. | `دƒ^خ± دƒ^خ² + دƒ^خ² دƒ^خ± = 0` (خ± â‰  خ²) | `Quantum/Pauli.lean` |

| `spinHalf_total_spin_squared` | `خ£ (إœ^(خ±))آ² = (3/4) آ· I`, i.e. `S(S+1)` with `S=1/2` | `Quantum/SpinHalf.lean` |

### Spin-1/2 rotation operators (Tasaki آ§2.1 eq. (2.1.26))

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, آ§2.1 eq. (2.1.26), p. 17 (closed form) and eq. (2.1.23),
p. 16 (`أ›_{2د€} = -1` for half-odd-integer spin).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `spinHalfRot1/2/3` | `أ›^(خ±)_خ¸ := cos(خ¸/2) آ· 1 - 2i آ· sin(خ¸/2) آ· إœ^(خ±)` | `Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` |
| `spinHalfRot1/2/3_zero` | `أ›^(خ±)_0 = 1` | `Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` |
| `spinHalfRot1/2/3_adjoint` | `(أ›^(خ±)_خ¸)â€  = أ›^(خ±)_{-خ¸}` | `Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` |

### Zâ‚‚ أ— Zâ‚‚ representation (Tasaki آ§2.1 eqs. (2.1.27)-(2.1.34))

The Zâ‚‚ أ— Zâ‚‚ structure is proved across files:
- S = 1/2 (projective, eq. (2.1.31)): `spinHalfRot*_pi_sq = -1`, anticommutation, products.
- S = 1 (genuine, eq. (2.1.27)): `spinOnePiRot*_sq = 1`, commutation.

See `Quantum/Z2Z2.lean` for the unified documentation.

### Spin-`S` operators (general S â‰¥ 0, parameterised by `N = 2S : â„•`)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body Systems*, آ§2.1 Problem 2.1.a (p. 15) and solution S.1 (p. 493).

Generic spin-`S` operators live on `Matrix (Fin (N + 1)) (Fin (N + 1)) â„‚`, with `N = 2S : â„•` (so `N = 1` â‡” `S = 1/2`, `N = 2` â‡” `S = 1`). Tracking issue #458 (Tasaki آ§2.1 P1d''' general-S generalisation).

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `spinSOp3` | `إœ^(3) := diag(N/2, N/2 - 1, â€¦, -N/2)` for `N : â„•` | `Quantum/SpinS/Operators.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus` / `spinSOpMinus` | raising/lowering operators with matrix entries `âˆڑ(kآ·(N âˆ’ k + 1))` (resp. `âˆڑ((N âˆ’ k)(k + 1))`) on the immediate sub/super-diagonal | `Quantum/SpinS/Operators.lean` |

Together with خ²-20 and خ²-21 this completes the standard SU(2) commutator algebra (Tasaki eq. (2.1.1)) for spin-`S` operators (خ²-22 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/CyclicCommutator31.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_mul_self` / `spinSDiagProj_mul_of_ne` | **Idempotence and orthogonality** of the diagonal projectors `P_k = |kâں©âں¨k|`: `P_k آ· P_k = P_k` and `P_i آ· P_j = 0` for `i â‰  j`. Combined with خ²-9 (`âˆ‘_k P_k = 1`) this gives the spectral decomposition of the identity for `إœ^{(3)}` (خ²-23 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/DiagProjOrtho.lean` |
| `aeval_diagonal` | **Polynomial evaluation at a diagonal matrix**: `aeval (Matrix.diagonal v) p = Matrix.diagonal (fun i => p.eval (v i))`. Foundational lemma for the Lagrange-interpolation step (خ²-25+) â€” lets us pull a polynomial in `إœ^{(3)}` (a diagonal matrix) through to its scalar action on each diagonal entry. Proof by `Polynomial.induction_on'` on monomials and addition (خ²-24 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/AevalDiagonal.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_eq_lagrange_aeval` | **Lagrange-interpolation formula for `P_k`**: `P_k = aeval (إœ^{(3)}) (Lagrange.basis Finset.univ (spinSOp3Eigen N) k)`, equivalently `P_k = âˆڈ_{j â‰  k} (إœ^{(3)} âˆ’ خ»_j â€¢ 1)/(خ»_k âˆ’ خ»_j)` with `خ»_j = (N : â„‚)/2 âˆ’ j.val`. Combines خ²-24 (`aeval` of diagonal) with mathlib's `Lagrange.eval_basis_self` / `eval_basis_of_ne`. Each diagonal projector is therefore a **polynomial in `إœ^{(3)}`**, which combined with خ²-9 (`âˆ‘ P_k = 1`) gives an explicit polynomial decomposition of `1ج‚` (خ²-25 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/LagrangeFormula.lean` |
| `spinSOpPlus_eq_one_add_I_smul_two` / `spinSOpMinus_eq_one_sub_I_smul_two` | **Inversion of the Cartesian definition**: `إœ^+ = إœ^{(1)} + i آ· إœ^{(2)}` and `إœ^- = إœ^{(1)} âˆ’ i آ· إœ^{(2)}`. The defining identities `إœ^{(1)} = (1/2)(إœ^+ + إœ^-)`, `إœ^{(2)} = (1/(2i))(إœ^+ âˆ’ إœ^-)` invert to express the ladder operators as **linear combinations** of the Hermitian Cartesian spin operators (خ²-26 of Issue #458) | `Quantum/SpinS/PMAsOneTwo.lean` |
| `spinSDiagProj_mem_adjoin_spinSOp3` / `spinSDiagProj_mem_adjoin` | **Diagonal projectors live in the algebra generated by the spin operators**: `P_k âˆˆ Algebra.adjoin â„‚ {إœ^{(3)}}` (and a fortiori `P_k âˆˆ Algebra.adjoin â„‚ {إœ^{(1)}, إœ^{(2)}, إœ^{(3)}}`). | `spinSOpPlus_mem_adjoin` / `spinSOpMinus_mem_adjoin` | **Ladder operators live in `Algebra.adjoin â„‚ {إœ^{(خ±)}}`**: `إœ^+, إœ^- âˆˆ Algebra.adjoin â„‚ {إœ^{(1)}, إœ^{(2)}, إœ^{(3)}}`. | `single_succ_mem_adjoin` / `single_succ_swap_mem_adjoin` | **Immediate-neighbor matrix units live in `Algebra.adjoin â„‚ {إœ^{(خ±)}}`**: `E_{i, i+1}, E_{i+1, i} âˆˆ Algebra.adjoin â„‚ {إœ^{(1)}, إœ^{(2)}, إœ^{(3)}}`. | `single_offset_succ_mem_adjoin` / `single_offset_succ_swap_mem_adjoin` | **Arbitrary stride-(k+1) matrix units live in `Algebra.adjoin â„‚ {إœ^{(خ±)}}`**: `E_{i, i+(k+1)}, E_{i+(k+1), i} âˆˆ Algebra.adjoin â„‚ {إœ^{(خ±)}}` for any `k`. | `matrix_single_mem_adjoin` | **Every matrix unit `E_{i,j}` lives in `Algebra.adjoin â„‚ {إœ^{(خ±)}}`**. | `matrix_mem_adjoin` / **`spinS_adjoin_eq_top`** | **ًںژ¯ Tasaki آ§2.1 Problem 2.1.a (P1d''') general-`S`**: every operator on the `(2S+1)`-dimensional spin-`S` Hilbert space `â„‚^{N+1}` is a polynomial in `{1ج‚, إœ^{(1)}, إœ^{(2)}, إœ^{(3)}}`. | `ManyBodyOpS` / `onSiteS` / `spinSSiteOp{1,2,3,Plus,Minus}` | **Multi-site spin-`S` operator space** indexed by configurations `دƒ : خ› â†’ Fin (N + 1)`, with the site-embedded operator `onSiteS i A` acting as `A` on site `i` and as the identity elsewhere; site-specialised `إœ_i^{(خ±)}, إœ_i^آ±`. | `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_spinHalfDot_mulVec` | **Time-reversal invariance of the bilinear `إœ_x آ· إœ_y`** (Tasaki آ§2.3): `خکج‚_tot ((إœ_x آ· إœ_y) v) = (إœ_x آ· إœ_y)(خکج‚_tot v)` â€” two equivariance `-1` factors cancel; sums per-axis | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_heisenbergHamiltonian_mulVec` | **Time-reversal invariance of the Heisenberg Hamiltonian** (Tasaki آ§2.3): for real coupling `J` (`conj(J(x,y)) = J(x,y)`), `خکج‚_tot ((H J) v) = (H J)(خکج‚_tot v)`. | `openChainCoupling_conj` / `periodicChainCoupling_conj` | every entry of `openChainCoupling N J` (resp. `periodicChainCoupling N J`) is real (under complex conjugation), since `J : â„‌` makes `(-(J : â„‚))` real-valued | `Quantum/HeisenbergChain.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_openChainHeisenberg_mulVec` / `_periodicChainHeisenberg_mulVec` / `_squareLatticeHeisenberg_mulVec` / `_squareTorusHeisenberg_mulVec` / `_cubicLatticeHeisenberg_mulVec` | concrete time-reversal invariance: the open / periodic chain, the 2D open square / torus, and the 3D cubic Heisenberg Hamiltonians all commute with `خکج‚_tot` for any real coupling `J : â„‌`. | `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_basisVec_upDown` / `_basisVec_basisSwap_upDown` | `خکج‚_tot |â†‘â†“âں© = -|â†“â†‘âں©` and `خکج‚_tot |â†“â†‘âں© = -|â†‘â†“âں©` on `Fin 2` | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_singlet` | the two-site spin singlet `|â†‘â†“âں© - |â†“â†‘âں©` is **time-reversal invariant** (Tasaki آ§2.3 / آ§A.3): being the SU(2) `S = 0` representation, it survives `خکج‚_tot` unchanged | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |
| `timeReversalSpinHalfMulti_triplet_zero` | the triplet `m = 0` state `|â†‘â†“âں© + |â†“â†‘âں©` is **anti-invariant** under `خکج‚_tot`: `خکج‚_tot (|â†‘â†“âں© + |â†“â†‘âں©) = -(|â†‘â†“âں© + |â†“â†‘âں©)` (the symmetric combination picks up a minus sign from the per-basis-vector flip) | `Quantum/TimeReversalMulti.lean` |

### Multi-body operator space (abstract lattice)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, آ§2.2, pp. 21-26 (tensor-product Hilbert space and site-local
operators). The lattice `خ›` is an arbitrary finite set with decidable
equality; specializing to `خ› = Fin N` recovers an `N`-site chain.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `ManyBodyOp خ›` | `Matrix (خ› â†’ Fin 2) (خ› â†’ Fin 2) â„‚` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite i A` | site-embedded operator at `i : خ›` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_isHermitian` | `A.IsHermitian â†’ (onSite i A).IsHermitian` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_add`, `onSite_sub`, `onSite_zero`, `onSite_smul`, `onSite_one` | linearity of the site embedding and `onSite i 1 = 1` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_mul_onSite_of_ne` | distinct-site commutation (Tasaki (2.2.6), `x â‰  y`, S = 1/2) | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `basisVec` / `onSite_mulVec_basisVec` | tensor-product basis states and their action under site operators (Tasaki (2.2.1)/(2.2.4)) | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_mul_onSite_same` | same-site product `onSite i A آ· onSite i B = onSite i (A آ· B)` (Tasaki (2.2.6), `x = y`) | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `onSite_commutator_same` | same-site commutator `[onSite i A, onSite i B] = onSite i [A, B]` | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |
| `Matrix.IsHermitian.mul_of_commute` | commuting Hermitians multiply Hermitian | `Quantum/ManyBody.lean` |

| `totalSpinHalfOp{Plus,Minus}_exp_commute_of_commute` | ladder version: `Commute A (إœ^آ±_tot) â†’ Commute A (exp(c â€¢ إœ^آ±_tot))` for any `c : â„‚` (useful for U(1) symmetry) | `Quantum/TotalSpin.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfRot{1,2,3}_conjTranspose_mul_self` | `(أ›^(خ±)_خ¸_tot)ل´´ * أ›^(خ±)_خ¸_tot = 1` (unitarity). Derived from `exp_mem_unitary_of_mem_skewAdjoint` after recognizing `-iخ¸ إœ_tot^(خ±)` as skew-adjoint | `Quantum/TotalSpin.lean` |
| `totalSpinHalfRot{1,2,3}_conj_eq_self_of_commute` | Tasaki eq. (2.2.13) finite form: `Commute A (إœ_tot^(خ±)) â†’ (أ›^(خ±)_خ¸_tot)ل´´ * A * أ›^(خ±)_خ¸_tot = A`. Combines `_commute_of_commute` with unitarity | `Quantum/TotalSpin.lean` |
| `IsInMagnetizationSubspace` | predicate for the magnetization-`M` eigenspace `H_M` (Tasaki eq. (2.2.9)/(2.2.10)) | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `magnetizationSubspace M` | the magnetization-`M` eigenspace as a `Submodule â„‚ ((خ› â†’ Fin 2) â†’ â„‚)` | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `basisVec_mem_magnetizationSubspace` | `|دƒâں© âˆˆ H_{|دƒ|/2}` â€” basis states lie in their magnetization subspace | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `magnetizationSubspace_disjoint` | distinct sectors `H_M âٹ“ H_{M'} = âٹ¥` (`M â‰  M'`) â€” eigenvalue uniqueness | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `iSup_magnetizationSubspace_eq_top` | `â¨†_M H_M = âٹ¤` â€” every vector decomposes as a sum across sectors | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `magnetizationSubspace_eq_eigenspace` | bridge `H_M = (إœ_tot^(3) as End).eigenspace M` (used to inherit `iSupIndep`) | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `magnetizationSubspace_iSupIndep` | `iSupIndep`: each sector is disjoint from the supremum of all others | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |
| `magnetizationSubspace_isInternal` | `DirectSum.IsInternal`: full direct-sum decomposition `H = âٹ•_M H_M` (Tasaki eqs. (2.2.9)/(2.2.10)) | `Quantum/MagnetizationSubspace.lean` |

### One-dimensional open-chain quantum Ising

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, آ§3.3 eq. (3.3.1), p. 55 (transverse-field Ising on an open
chain). Our formalization uses the Pauli convention `دƒ = 2آ·S` and an
explicit bond coupling `J`.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `quantumIsingHamiltonian N J h` | `H = -J خ£ دƒ^z_i دƒ^z_{i+1} - h خ£ دƒ^x_i` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |

| `spinZDot x y` | the Ising bond operator `دƒ^z_x آ· دƒ^z_y` (generic in `خ›`) | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `spinZDot_isHermitian` | each bond operator is Hermitian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianGeneric (J : خ› â†’ خ› â†’ â„‚) (h : â„‚)` | **graph-friendly** Ising Hamiltonian `خ£ J(x,y) دƒ^z_x دƒ^z_y âˆ’ h خ£ دƒ^x_x` for any finite `خ›` and pairwise coupling `J`; specialises to chain / graph / lattice via the choice of `J` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianGeneric_isHermitian` | Hermitian for entry-wise real `J` and real `h` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianOnGraph G J h` | graph wrapper: `isingHamiltonianGeneric (couplingOf G J) h`; double-sum convention matches Heisenberg-on-graph | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingHamiltonianOnGraph_isHermitian` | Hermitian for real `J, h` | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingGibbsStateOnGraph G خ² J h` | Gibbs state of the graph-built Ising Hamiltonian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `isingGibbsStateOnGraph_isHermitian` / `isingGibbsStateOnGraph_commute_hamiltonian` | Hermiticity (real `J, h`) and commute with the Hamiltonian | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |
| `LatticeSystem.Lattice.sum_pathGraph_forward` / `sum_pathGraph_backward` / `sum_pathGraph_adj` | sum-decomposition helpers for `pathGraph (N+1)` adjacency: `خ£_{x,y}` over ordered adjacent pairs = `خ£_{i:Fin N} (f i.cs i.s + f i.s i.cs)` | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `pathGraphParityColoring` / `pathGraph_isBipartite` | parity-based 2-colouring of `pathGraph (N + 1)` (`i â†¦ i.val % 2`) and the corresponding `IsBipartite` proof. Underpins the Nأ©el state (`Quantum/NeelState.lean`) and the Marshall-Lieb-Mattis theorem (Tasaki آ§2.5) | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `cycleGraphEvenParityColoring` / `cycleGraph_even_isBipartite` | parity-based 2-colouring of the even cycle `cycleGraph (2 * K + 2)` and the corresponding `IsBipartite` proof. Wrap-around case `(2K+1) + 1 â‰، 0` still flips parity because the cycle length is even (odd cycles are not bipartite) | `Lattice/Graph.lean` |
| `quantumIsingHamiltonian_eq_isingHamiltonianGeneric` | **generic-N bridge**: `quantumIsingHamiltonian N J h = isingHamiltonianGeneric (couplingOf (pathGraph (N+1)) (-J/2)) h`. The proof itself is the robust regression test | `Quantum/IsingChain.lean` |

### Gibbs state (Tasaki آ§3.3)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, آ§3.3.

All theorems in this module are fully proved with **zero `sorry`**.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `gibbsExp خ² H` | `exp(-خ²H) := Matrix.exp (-خ² â€¢ H)` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_isHermitian` | `exp(-خ²H)` is Hermitian (when `H` is Hermitian) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_zero` | `exp(-0آ·H) = 1` (Tasaki آ§3.3, pp. 75â€“78) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_add` | `exp(-(خ²â‚پ+خ²â‚‚)H) = exp(-خ²â‚پH) آ· exp(-خ²â‚‚H)` (one-parameter group) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_add_of_commute_hamiltonians` | `exp(-خ²(Hâ‚پ+Hâ‚‚)) = exp(-خ²Hâ‚پ) آ· exp(-خ²Hâ‚‚)` for commuting `Hâ‚پ, Hâ‚‚` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_neg_mul_self` | `exp(خ²H) آ· exp(-خ²H) = 1` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_self_mul_neg` | `exp(-خ²H) آ· exp(خ²H) = 1` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_isUnit` | `exp(-خ²H)` is invertible | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsExp_ne_zero` | `exp(-خ²H) â‰  0` (corollary of `gibbsExp_isUnit`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_ne_zero` | `دپ_خ² â‰  0` when `Z(خ²) â‰  0` | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |
| `gibbsState_inv` | `(دپ_خ²)âپ»آ¹ = Z(خ²) آ· e^{خ²H}` when `Z(خ²) â‰  0` (general matrix inverse, generalises `gibbsState_zero_inv`) | `Quantum/GibbsState.lean` |

### Heisenberg chain (Tasaki آ§3.5)

Primary reference: Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, آ§3.5, p. 89.

### Perron-Frobenius theorem (`Math/PerronFrobenius.lean`, `Math/PerronFrobeniusPrimitive.lean`, `Math/CollatzWielandt.lean`, `Math/PerronFrobeniusMain.lean`)

### Spin-`S` Marshallâ€“Liebâ€“Mattis on the magnetization sector (Tasaki آ§2.5 Theorem 2.2 generic S, sector form)

Generic-spin (`N = 2S`) version of Tasaki آ§2.5 Theorem 2.2 applied to the
**magnetization-`M` sector** of the un-dressed antiferromagnetic
Heisenberg Hamiltonian on a bipartite graph. The sector subtype
`magConfigS V N M := { دƒ : V â†’ Fin (N + 1) // magSumS دƒ = M }` is the
natural index type since the dressed Heisenberg matrix is irreducible
on each sector. All theorems live in
`Quantum/SpinS/DressedMatrixOnMagSector.lean`. Tracked in Issue #412.

| Lean name | Statement |
|---|---|
| `magConfigS V N M` | sector subtype of magnetization-`M` configurations (`Quantum/SpinS/MagConfig.lean`) |
| `RaiseLowerStepSMagSector G دƒ د„` / `RaiseLowerReachableSMagSector G` | bipartite raise/lower step lifted to `magConfigS` and its reflexive transitive closure (`Quantum/SpinS/MagConfig.lean`) |
| `raiseLowerReachableSMagSector_bipartiteCompleteGraph` | any two configurations in the same sector are reachable via raise/lower steps under the bipartite-intermediate hypothesis (Tasaki آ§2.5 Property (iii) generic-S form) |
| `shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector A J N c M` | shifted dressed Heisenberg matrix `cآ·1 - dressed_re` restricted to the sector via `Matrix.submatrix Subtype.val Subtype.val`, the input to PF irreducibility |
| `dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector A J N M` | dressed Heisenberg real-form matrix restricted to the sector |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector J N M` | un-dressed Heisenberg real-form matrix restricted to the sector |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector J N M` | un-dressed Heisenberg COMPLEX matrix restricted to the sector |
| `isIrreducible_shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector` | `Matrix.IsIrreducible` for the shifted sector matrix (Tasaki آ§2.5 خ³-3 final, MLM PF input) |
| `exists_positive_eigenvector_shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector` | PF eigenvector existence for the shifted sector matrix (`r > 0`, `v > 0` componentwise) |
| `pos_eigenvec_unique_shiftedDressedSReMatrixOnMagSector` | PF eigenvector uniqueness on the shifted sector matrix (Tasaki آ§2.5 nondegeneracy) |
| `exists_positive_eigenvector_dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector` | PF on the dressed sector matrix at eigenvalue `c - r` (Tasaki آ§2.5 dressed-form ground state) |
| `pos_eigenvec_unique_dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector` | dressed sector eigenvector uniqueness at fixed eigenvalue (PR #856) |
| `pos_eigenvec_eigenvalue_unique_dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector` | dressed sector positive eigenvectors share the same eigenvalue (Rayleigh identity for symmetric matrices, PR #856) |
| `dressedHeisenbergSReMatrix_eq_marshallSign_mul_heisenberg` / `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrix_eq_marshallSign_mul_dressed` | matrix relations `dressed = signآ·signآ·heis` and inverse via `signآ² = 1` (PR #853) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_of_dressed_eigenvec` | Marshall sign conjugation of dressed sector eigenvector to un-dressed Heisenberg sector eigenvector (PR #853) |
| `dressedHeisenbergSReMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_of_heis_eigenvec` | inverse Marshall conjugation (PR #854) |
| `exists_marshallSign_eigenvector_heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector` | un-dressed Heisenberg sector ground-state existence with Marshall sign structure (PR #853) |
| `marshallPositive_eigenvec_unique_heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector` | un-dressed Heisenberg sector Marshall-positive eigenvector uniqueness at fixed eigenvalue (PR #854) |
| `marshallPositive_eigenvec_eigenvalue_unique_heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector` | un-dressed Heisenberg sector Marshall-positive eigenvalue uniqueness (PR #856) |
| `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_groundState` | bundled Tasaki آ§2.5 Theorem 2.2 (existence + same-eigenvalue uniqueness, PR #855) |
| `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_groundState_full` | strongest bundled Tasaki آ§2.5 Theorem 2.2: existence + forced eigenvalue uniqueness + eigenvector uniqueness (PR #859) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector_isHermitian` | complex sector matrix is Hermitian for real coupling (PR #858) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector_apply_eq_ofReal` | for real coupling, complex sector entries equal real-form entries embedded in `â„‚` (PR #857) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_ofReal` | real â†’ complex eigenvector lift (PR #858) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianSReMatrixOnMagSector_mulVec_re_of_complex_eigenvec` | complex â†’ real real-part extraction (PR #861) |
| `exists_marshallSign_complexEigenvector_heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector` | complex-form Tasaki آ§2.5 Theorem 2.2 ground-state existence on the un-dressed quantum Heisenberg sector matrix (PR #860) |
| `marshallPositive_complexEigenvec_re_unique_heisenbergHamiltonianSMatrixOnMagSector` | complex-form Marshall-positive uniqueness via real-part extraction (PR #862) |
| `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_complexGroundState_full` | strongest bundled Tasaki آ§2.5 Theorem 2.2 on the complex sector matrix (PR #863) |

The complex-form `marshallLiebMattis_spinS_heisenbergSector_complexGroundState_full`
is the COMPLEX-Hilbert-space form of Tasaki آ§2.5 Theorem 2.2 in the
magnetization sector: the ground state of the un-dressed quantum
Heisenberg Hamiltonian restricted to the sector is unique (up to a
positive real scalar in its real part) and has the Marshall sign
structure `خ¦ دƒ := ((sign A دƒ.1).re * v دƒ : â„‚)` with `v > 0`.

References: H. Tasaki, *Physics and Mathematics of Quantum Many-Body
Systems*, Springer 2020, آ§2.5 Theorem 2.2 (pp. 39â€“43); E. Seneta,
*Non-negative Matrices and Markov Chains* (3rd ed.), Springer 2006,
آ§1.2 (pp. 27â€“28) for the underlying Perronâ€“Frobenius theorem.

### Spin-`S` saturated ferromagnetic state (Tasaki آ§2.4 generalised)

Generic-spin (`N = 2S`) version of Tasaki آ§2.4 P1i for the
**saturated ferromagnet**: the all-aligned (constant-spin) basis
state `|دƒ_âٹ¤âں© = âٹ—_x |câں©` with `دƒ x = c` for all `x : V`. The two
extremal weights `c = 0` (highest weight, "all up") and
`c = Fin.last N` (lowest weight, "all down") are the highest- and
lowest-weight vectors of the `J_tot = |V|آ·S = |V|آ·N/2` irreducible
SU(2) representation in the multi-site Hilbert space. Tracked in
Issue #412; assembled in PRs #875â€“#879. All theorems live in
`Quantum/SpinS/AllAlignedState.lean`.

| Lean name | Statement |
|---|---|
| `allAlignedConfigS V N c` | constant configuration `دƒ x = c` (PR #875) |
| `allAlignedStateS V N c` | basis state at constant `c`, equal to `basisVecS (allAlignedConfigS V N c)` (PR #875) |
| `magSumS_allAlignedConfigS` | `magSumS = |V|آ·c.val` (PR #875) |
| `magEigenvalueS_allAlignedConfigS` | `magEigenvalueS = |V|آ·N/2 âˆ’ |V|آ·c` (PR #875) |
| `totalSpinSOp3_mulVec_allAlignedStateS` | `إœ^z_tot آ· |câں© = (|V|آ·N/2 âˆ’ |V|آ·c) آ· |câں©` for any `c` (PR #875) |
| `magSumS_allAlignedConfigS_zero` | `c = 0` âں¹ `magSumS = 0` (PR #875) |
| `magSumS_pos_of_ne_allAlignedConfigS_zero` | the all-up configuration is the **unique** `magSumS = 0` configuration (PR #875) |
| `magSumS_allAlignedConfigS_last` | `c = Fin.last N` âں¹ `magSumS = |V|آ·N` (PR #876) |
| `magSumS_lt_card_mul_of_ne_allAlignedConfigS_last` | the all-down configuration is the unique configuration with `magSumS = |V|آ·N` (PR #876) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero` | the **all-up state is a Heisenberg eigenvector for ANY coupling** â€” magnetization conservation `[H, إœ^z_tot] = 0` + uniqueness of the M=0 configuration (PR #875) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_zero_eigenvalue` | explicit Heisenberg eigenvalue formula on all-up: `خ£_x J(x,x)آ·N(N+2)/4 + خ£_{xâ‰ y} J(x,y)آ·Nآ²/4` (PR #875) |
| `heisenbergHamiltonianS_mulVec_allAlignedStateS_last` / `_eigenvalue` | symmetric c = N (all-down) Heisenberg eigenvector + same eigenvalue formula (PR #876) |

### Single-mode fermion (P2 skeleton)

Phase 2 entry point: the canonical anticommutation algebra of a single
fermion mode acting on `â„‚آ²` with computational basis
`|0âں©` (vacuum) and `|1âں©` (occupied).

| `fermionMultiAnnihilation_anticomm_zero_pos` | **general cross-site CAR `{c_0, c_k} = 0`** for every `k : Fin (N+1)` with `0 < k.val` â€” generalises the `_zero_one` / `_zero_two_general` specialisations. | `fermionMultiCreation_anticomm_zero_pos` | dual `{c_0â€ , c_kâ€ } = 0` for every `k : Fin (N+1)` with `0 < k.val` (adjoint of the above) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `fermionMultiAnnihilation_creation_anticomm_zero_pos` | mixed `{c_0, c_kâ€ } = 0` for every `k : Fin (N+1)` with `0 < k.val` â€” same inductive argument on the JW string anticommutator (the site-`k` factor is `دƒ^-_k` instead of `دƒ^+_k`; JW-string part is unchanged) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `fermionMultiCreation_annihilation_anticomm_zero_pos` | mixed dual `{c_0â€ , c_k} = 0` for every `k : Fin (N+1)` with `0 < k.val` (adjoint of the above) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `jwStringExceptAt` / `jwString_eq_onSite_mul_jwStringExceptAt` / `jwStringExceptAt_commute_onSite` | private factorisation helpers for the Jordan-Wigner string at an interior site (#210): for `i.val < j.val`, `jwString N j = onSite i pauliZ * jwStringExceptAt N j i`, and `jwStringExceptAt N j i` commutes with every single-site operator at site `i` | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `jwString_anticomm_onSite_pos_spinHalfOpPlus` | operator-level anticommutator `{دƒ^+_i, jwString N j} = 0` for every `i j : Fin (N+1)` with `i.val < j.val` â€” generalises `jwString_anticomm_onSite_zero_spinHalfOpPlus` (i = 0 case) to arbitrary interior `i`; building block for the fully general cross-site CAR `{c_i, c_j} = 0` (#210) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `jwString_anticomm_onSite_pos_spinHalfOpMinus` | companion `{دƒ^-_i, jwString N j} = 0` for every `i < j` (via `conjTranspose` of the `دƒ^+` version) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `jwString_commute_jwString` | any two Jordan-Wigner strings `jwString N i` and `jwString N j` commute (both are noncommutative products of `دƒ^z` over distinct sites) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `fermionMultiAnnihilation_anticomm_lt` | **fully general cross-site CAR `{c_i, c_j} = 0` for `i < j`** (#210) on `Fin (N + 1)`. Proof: reduce via `jwString_anticomm_onSite_pos_spinHalfOpPlus` to an identity involving `JW_i آ· JW_j = JW_j آ· JW_i` (via `jwString_commute_jwString`), which makes the sum collapse | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `fermionMultiCreation_anticomm_lt` | dual `{c_iâ€ , c_jâ€ } = 0` for `i < j` (adjoint of the above) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `fermionMultiAnnihilation_creation_anticomm_lt` | mixed `{c_i, c_jâ€ } = 0` for `i < j` â€” same structure as `_anticomm_lt` but with `دƒ^-_j` at site `j` | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `fermionMultiCreation_annihilation_anticomm_lt` | mixed dual `{c_iâ€ , c_j} = 0` for `i < j` (adjoint of the above) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `spinHalfOpPlus_mul_self` / `spinHalfOpPlus_mul_spinHalfOpMinus_mul_spinHalfOpPlus` | Pauli helper identities `دƒ^+ دƒ^+ = 0` and `دƒ^+ دƒ^- دƒ^+ = دƒ^+` | `Quantum/SpinHalfBasis.lean` |
| `fermionMultiNumber_commutator_fermionMultiAnnihilation_self` | `[n_i, c_i] = -c_i` (number / annihilation commutator) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |

#### Hubbard spin symmetry â€” full SU(2) invariance (Tasaki آ§9.3.3)

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|

#### Hubbard all-up-spin state and saturated ferromagnetism (Tasaki آ§11.1.1)

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `hubbardAllUpState N` | fully spin-polarised basis vector: all spin-up orbitals occupied, spin-down empty (even JW indices = 1, odd = 0) | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/AllUpState.lean` |
| `fermionUpNumber_mulVec_allUpState` | `n_{i,â†‘} آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں© = |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں©` â€” each spin-up number operator acts as identity on the all-up state | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/AllUpState.lean` |
| `fermionDownNumber_mulVec_allUpState` | `n_{i,â†“} آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں© = 0` â€” no spin-down electrons; key to the vanishing of `H_int` | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/AllUpState.lean` |
| `hubbardOnSiteInteraction_mulVec_allUpState` | `H_int آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں© = 0` â€” no double occupancy in the fully-polarised state (Tasaki آ§11.1.1, p. 373; eq. (10.1.5), p. 344) | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/AllUpState.lean` |
| `hubbardHamiltonian_mulVec_allUpState` | `H آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں© = H_hop آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں©` â€” the Hubbard model in the all-up sector reduces to a non-interacting hopping problem | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/AllUpState.lean` |
| `fermionDownAnnihilation_mulVec_allUpState` | `c_{i,â†“} آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں© = 0` â€” spin-down annihilation kills the all-up state (odd JW index unoccupied, so دƒâپ؛ maps it to 0) (Tasaki آ§11.1.1, p. 373) | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/AllUpState.lean` |
| `fermionUpCreation_mulVec_allUpState` | `câ€ _{i,â†‘} آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں© = 0` â€” spin-up creation kills the all-up state (even JW index already occupied, so دƒâپ» maps it to 0) (Tasaki آ§11.1.1, p. 373) | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/AllUpState.lean` |
| `hubbardKinetic_mulVec_allUpState` | `H_hop آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں© = (خ£_i t i i) â€¢ |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں©` â€” hopping eigenvalue: off-diagonal terms vanish by CAR anticommutation, diagonal terms give 1 each (Tasaki آ§11.1.1, p. 373) | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/AllUpState.lean` |
| `hubbardHamiltonian_mulVec_allUpState_eigenstate` | `H آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں© = (خ£_i t i i) â€¢ |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں©` â€” full Hamiltonian eigenstate: combines `H_hop` eigenvalue and `H_int آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں© = 0` (Tasaki آ§11.1.1, p. 373; eq. (10.1.5), p. 344) | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/AllUpState.lean` |
| `fermionTotalSpinSquared` | total-spin Casimir `(إœ_tot)آ² = إœâپ»إœâپ؛ + إœ_z(إœ_z+1)` | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/SaturatedFerromagnetism.lean` |
| `fermionTotalUpNumber_mulVec_allUpState` | `N_â†‘ آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں© = (N+1) â€¢ |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں©` | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/SaturatedFerromagnetism.lean` |
| `fermionTotalDownNumber_mulVec_allUpState` | `N_â†“ آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں© = 0` | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/SaturatedFerromagnetism.lean` |
| `fermionTotalSpinZ_mulVec_allUpState` | `إœ^z_tot آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں© = ((N+1)/2) â€¢ |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں©` | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/SaturatedFerromagnetism.lean` |
| `fermionTotalSpinPlus_mulVec_allUpState` | `إœâپ؛_tot آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں© = 0` â€” highest-weight state; no down-spin to raise | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/SaturatedFerromagnetism.lean` |
| `fermionTotalSpinSquared_mulVec_allUpState` | `(إœ_tot)آ² آ· |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں© = S_max(S_max+1) â€¢ |â†‘â€¦â†‘âں©` where `S_max = (N+1)/2` (Tasaki آ§11.1.1, p. 372) | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/SaturatedFerromagnetism.lean` |
| `fermionTotalSpinSquared_commute_hubbardHamiltonian` | `[(إœ_tot)آ², H] = 0` â€” Casimir commutes with H (from SU(2) invariance, Tasaki آ§9.3.3) | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/SaturatedFerromagnetism.lean` |
| `isSaturatedFerromagnet` | **Definition 11.1** â€” Lean predicate: there exists a ground-state energy `Eâ‚€` such that every nonzero `H`-eigenvector with eigenvalue `Eâ‚€` is a `(إœ_tot)آ²`-eigenvector with eigenvalue `S_max(S_max+1)` (Tasaki آ§11.1.1, p. 372) | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/SaturatedFerromagnetism.lean` |
| `fermionTotalSpinZ_commutator_fermionTotalSpinMinus` | `[إœ^z_tot, إœ^-_tot] = -إœ^-_tot` â€” SU(2) algebra relation; follows from site-wise `[إœ_z, câ€ _{i,â†“}c_{i,â†‘}] = -(câ€ _{i,â†“}c_{i,â†‘})` (Tasaki آ§9.3.3, p. 332) | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/SaturatedFerromagnetism.lean` |
| `fermionTotalSpinMinus_mulVec_preserves_hamiltonian_eigenvalue` | if `Hآ·v = Eآ·v` then `Hآ·(إœ^-آ·v) = Eآ·(إœ^-آ·v)` â€” applying `إœ^-` preserves Hamiltonian eigenvalues; follows from `[إœ^-, H] = 0` (Tasaki آ§11.1.1, p. 373) | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/SaturatedFerromagnetism.lean` |
| `fermionTotalSpinZ_mulVec_spinMinus_step` | if `إœ_zآ·v = mآ·v` then `إœ_zآ·(إœ^-آ·v) = (m-1)آ·(إœ^-آ·v)` â€” applying `إœ^-` decrements `إœ_z` eigenvalue by 1; follows from `[إœ^z, إœ^-] = -إœ^-` (Tasaki آ§2.4, eq. (2.4.9); آ§11.1.1, p. 373) | `Fermion/JordanWigner/Hubbard/SaturatedFerromagnetism.lean` |

| `hubbardKineticOnGraph N G J` | spinful Hubbard kinetic operator from a `SimpleGraph G` and edge weight `J` | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `hubbardKineticOnGraph_commute_fermionTotalNumber` / `hubbardKineticOnGraph_isHermitian` | charge conservation always; Hermiticity for real `J` | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `hubbardHamiltonianOnGraph N G J U` | full Hubbard Hamiltonian from a graph + on-site coupling | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |

| `hubbardChainHamiltonian N J U` | the canonical 1D nearest-neighbour Hubbard chain `âˆ’J خ£_{دƒ,âں¨i,jâں©} c_{iدƒ}â€  c_{jدƒ} + U خ£_i n_{iâ†‘} n_{iâ†“}` (built from `pathGraph (N+1)`) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `hubbardChainHamiltonian_isHermitian` / `hubbardChainHamiltonian_commute_fermionTotalNumber` | Hermiticity (real `J, U`) and charge conservation | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `hubbardHamiltonianOnGraph_mulVec_vacuum` / `hubbardChainHamiltonian_mulVec_vacuum` | both graph-built Hubbard Hamiltonians annihilate the JW vacuum | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `hubbardChainGibbsState N خ² J U` | Gibbs state of the 1D Hubbard chain | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `hubbardChainGibbsState_isHermitian` / `hubbardChainGibbsState_commute_hamiltonian` | Hermiticity (real `J, U`) and commute with the Hamiltonian | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `hubbardCycleGibbsState_commute_hamiltonian` | the periodic Hubbard Gibbs state commutes with the periodic Hubbard Hamiltonian (companion of the open-chain version, free corollary of `gibbsState_commute_hamiltonian`) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `hubbardChainGibbsExpectation_zero` / `_im_of_isHermitian` / `_commutator_hamiltonian` / `_hamiltonian_im` / `_hamiltonian_pow_im` / `hubbardChain_partitionFn_im` / `_ofReal_re_eq` / `hubbardChainGibbsState_pow_trace` | open-chain Hubbard expectation companions (خ² = 0 closed form, Hermitian-observable real, conservation, energy / energy-power expectations real, partition function real, real-cast, Rأ©nyi-n trace) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |
| `hubbardCycleGibbsExpectation_zero` / `_im_of_isHermitian` / `_commutator_hamiltonian` / `_hamiltonian_im` / `_hamiltonian_pow_im` / `hubbardCycle_partitionFn_im` / `_ofReal_re_eq` / `hubbardCycleGibbsState_pow_trace` | periodic Hubbard chain expectation companions (same family as the open chain) | `Fermion/JordanWigner.lean` |

## Continuum-limit roadmap

The project's long-term goals include the `د†^4` / Ising continuum
limit and lattice-QCD-style formalisations, both of which are defined
as limits `a â†’ 0` of families of finite-spacing lattice systems. A
survey of the gap between the current finite-volume matrix framework
and what the continuum limit actually demands was recorded during
Phase A scoping (consulted codex twice on scope and design choices)
and proposes the four phases below.

**Phase A (current, this PR)**. Add a **thin type-level tag**
`class LatticeWithSpacing (خ› : Type*) where spacing : â„‌â‰¥0`
so that a lattice spacing `a : â„‌â‰¥0` can be attached to `خ›` as
metadata. Provide the default instance `Fin (N + 1)` with
`spacing := 1` so every pre-existing Hamiltonian in the library is
`rfl`-equivalent to its `spacing := 1` specialisation. No geometry,
no rescaling, no continuum object.

**Phase B (deferred)**. Lattice sequences `خ›_n` with
`spacing a_n â†’ 0`, rescaling of coupling constants
(`J_n = ؤ¥ آ· a_n^{-2+d}` etc.), and lattice-point embeddings in
`â„‌^d`. Introduce when a concrete theorem (e.g. Osterwalder-Schrader,
a specific block-spin transformation) requires iterating over a
spacing sequence.

**Phase C (deferred)**. Operator-valued distribution / GNS /
Hilbert-space infrastructure to house the continuum limit itself.
Per codex (2026-04-22), we do **not** generalise
`ManyBodyOp خ› = Matrix _ _ â„‚` to a type class preemptively: existing
proofs depend on Matrix-specific API (`conjTranspose`, `exp`,
`trace`, `mulVec`, entry formulas), and the right abstraction becomes
clear only once a second concrete backend (infinite-volume Hilbert
space, quasi-local C*-algebra) is in place.

**Phase D (deferred)**. Coupling-constant running
`g : â„‌â‰¥0 â†’ â„‌` and renormalisation-group transformations. Follows
phases B-C.

| Lean name | Statement | File |
|---|---|---|
| `LatticeWithSpacing` | `class LatticeWithSpacing (خ› : Type*) where spacing : â„‌â‰¥0` â€” thin type-level tag recording the lattice spacing `a : â„‌â‰¥0` of a vertex type | `Lattice/Scale.lean` |
| `spacingOf` | `spacingOf خ› := LatticeWithSpacing.spacing` â€” named accessor | `Lattice/Scale.lean` |
| `instLatticeWithSpacingFinSucc` | default `spacing := 1` instance for `Fin (N + 1)`, making every existing Hamiltonian `rfl`-equivalent to the unit-spacing specialisation | `Lattice/Scale.lean` |
| `spacing_fin_succ` / `spacingOf_fin_succ` | `spacing = 1` computed at `Fin (N + 1)` | `Lattice/Scale.lean` |
| `instLatticeWithSpacingInt` | default `spacing := 1` instance for `â„¤` (infinite chain â€” matches `integerChainGraph`) | `Lattice/Scale.lean` |
| `instLatticeWithSpacingIntSq` | default `spacing := 1` instance for `â„¤ أ— â„¤` (infinite 2D square lattice â€” matches `integerSquareLatticeGraph`) | `Lattice/Scale.lean` |
| `spacing_int` / `spacingOf_int` / `spacing_int_sq` / `spacingOf_int_sq` | `spacing = 1` computed at `â„¤`, `â„¤ أ— â„¤` | `Lattice/Scale.lean` |

## Open items / axioms

The following Tasaki آ§2.1 / آ§2.2 items are **not yet fully proved**.
They are tracked here so that future PRs can pick them up and replace
each axiom by a proof (or fill in the deferred construction).

### ~~TODO (P1d''') â€” Problem 2.1.a for general `S â‰¥ 1`~~ **DONE**

**Statement (Tasaki p.15)**: For any spin `S`, every operator on the
single-site Hilbert space `h_0 = â„‚^{2S+1}` (i.e. every `(2S+1) أ— (2S+1)`
matrix) can be written as a polynomial in `1ج‚, إœ^(1), إœ^(2), إœ^(3)`.

**Status**: Done in general spin-`S` form (Issue #458 closed in PR #490).
The headline theorem `LatticeSystem.Quantum.spinS_adjoin_eq_top` proves

```
Algebra.adjoin â„‚ {إœ^(1) N, إœ^(2) N, إœ^(3) N}
  = (âٹ¤ : Subalgebra â„‚ (Matrix (Fin (N+1)) (Fin (N+1)) â„‚))
```

via Tasaki solution S.1: diagonal projectors `P_k` are Lagrange-interpolation
polynomials in `إœ^{(3)}` (`spinSDiagProj_eq_lagrange_aeval`); off-diagonal
matrix units `E_{i,j}` are products of ladder-step units
(`single_offset_succ_{,swap_}mem_adjoin`); the entry-wise decomposition
`M = âˆ‘_{i,j} M_{i,j} â€¢ E_{i,j}` then closes the spanning. The earlier
concrete-case modules `pauliBasis` (`S = 1/2`) and `spinOne_decomposition`
(`S = 1`) remain as illustrative specialisations.

### ~~TODO â€” Tasaki Problem 2.2.c (SU(2) non-invariance / averaged state)~~ **DONE**

**Statement (Tasaki p.23, eq. (2.2.15))**: An explicit averaged state
of the form

```
(1/4د€) âˆ«â‚€^{2د€} dد† âˆ«â‚€^د€ dخ¸ sin خ¸ آ· أ›^(3)_د† آ· أ›^(2)_خ¸ آ· |â†‘â‚پâں©|â†“â‚‚âں©
```

equals (up to phase) the singlet `(1/âˆڑ2)(|â†‘â‚پâں©|â†“â‚‚âں© - |â†“â‚پâں©|â†‘â‚‚âں©)`. The
problem asks to verify this and to characterize states that fail to be
SU(2)-invariant.

**Status**: Formally proved with zero `sorry` in `Quantum/SU2Integral.lean`
as `problem_2_2_c`. The proof integrates over the Euler-angle parameter space
using `integral_cexp_I_mul_zero_two_pi`, `integral_cexp_neg_I_mul_zero_two_pi`,
and the half-angle trig integrals established in earlier PRs. See
`Quantum/SpinHalfRotation.lean` for `spinHalfRot3_mul_spinHalfRot2_mulVec_spinHalfDown`
and `Quantum/SU2Integral.lean` for all supporting lemmas.

### TODO â€” Tasaki آ§2.5 antiferromagnetic deferred items (issue [#240](https://github.com/phasetr/lattice-system/issues/240))

The antiferromagnetic Heisenberg / Nأ©el state machinery in
Tasaki آ§2.5 is largely formalised (chain / 2D / 3D Nأ©el states +
per-bond expectations `-1/4` + generic graph-centric `neelStateOf`
+ Marshall sign machinery + time-reversal action; see Roadmap row
P1k above). The following subitems remain deferred (large
mathematical work):

- **Marshall-Lieb-Mattis Theorem 2.2** (uniqueness + sign
  structure of the AFM ground state). Requires a Perron-Frobenius
  argument on the Marshall-rotated basis.
- **Problem 2.5.a** (single-cluster ground-state energy
  `-S(1+zS)` for general spin `S` and coordination `z`).
  Requires general-spin infrastructure (P1d''' above is now done in PR #490; this remains for the آ§2.5-specific cluster argument).
- **Problem 2.5.b** (lower bound on `E_GS` via 2.5.a).
- **Problem 2.5.c** (single-site expectation `âں¨إœ_xâں© = 0` in the
  AFM ground state).
- **Problem 2.5.d** (two-spin correlation under MLM).

The generic graph-centric `neelStateOf` (Phase 3 PR #331) is the
foundation on which these will be built when general-spin and
Perron-Frobenius infrastructure becomes available.

### TODO â€” remove remaining 7 per-theorem linter suppressions (issue [#377](https://github.com/phasetr/lattice-system/issues/377))

Phase 4 substantially closed `lake build` warnings (zero warnings
+ zero errors as of 2026-04-23), with the exception of 7
per-theorem `set_option linter.{flexible,unusedTactic,unusedSimpArgs} false in`
blocks (4 in `SpinOne{Basis,Decomp}`, 3 in
`SpinHalfRotation/Conjugation`). All are comment-justified and
listed in the [Deprecation window](deprecations.html#remaining-linter-suppressions)
page. Removal requires interactive `simp?` per sub-case.

  CI job was consistently slow (often >1h). To build the API docs
  locally, run
  `lake build +Mathlib:docs` or consult the
  [doc-gen4 README](https://github.com/leanprover-community/doc-gen4).
  The CI job is commented out in
  `.github/workflows/lean_action_ci.yml` with a note on how to
  re-enable.
